Task instruction sent to agent 
# Bug Investigation: Multi-Device U2F Authentication Limited to Single Token

**Repository:** gravitational/teleport
**Task Type:** Find and Prove (write a regression test)

## Reported Issue

Users who have registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport report that during login, only one of their registered devices is recognized. The authentication flow presents a challenge for only a single device, preventing users from selecting which hardware token to use.

Specifically:

1. **Single-device lock-in**: After registering multiple U2F tokens via the MFA management flow, attempting to log in only issues a challenge for one device. The system should present challenges for all registered tokens so the user can tap whichever device is available.

2. **MFA device management gaps**: Operations for adding, listing, and removing MFA devices (both U2F and TOTP) do not correctly handle the transition from single-device to multi-device authentication. For example, deleting one device when multiple are registered may behave unexpectedly.

3. **Client/server version compatibility**: Older clients connecting to a newer server (and vice versa) may fail to negotiate the correct U2F challenge format, causing authentication errors during version upgrades.

## Your Task

1. Investigate the codebase to find the root cause of these multi-device U2F authentication limitations
2. Write a regression test as a single file at `/workspace/regression_test.go`
3. Your test must be self-contained and runnable with `go test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s /workspace/regression_test.go`

## Constraints

- Do NOT fix the bug — only write a test that demonstrates it
- Your test must fail on the current (buggy) code for the RIGHT reason
- The test should cover at least: multi-device U2F challenge generation and client/server compatibility
- Test timeout: 60 seconds

   828→func (a *Server) U2FSignRequest(user string, password []byte) (*u2f.AuthenticateChallenge, error) {
   829→	ctx := context.TODO()
   830→	cap, err := a.GetAuthPreference()
   831→	if err != nil {
   832→		return nil, trace.Wrap(err)
   833→	}
   834→
   835→	u2fConfig, err := cap.GetU2F()
   836→	if err != nil {
   837→		return nil, trace.Wrap(err)
   838→	}
   839→
   840→	err = a.WithUserLock(user, func() error {
   841→		return a.CheckPasswordWOToken(user, password)
   842→	})
   843→	if err != nil {
   844→		return nil, trace.Wrap(err)
   845→	}
   846→
   847→	// TODO(awly): mfa: support challenge with multiple devices.
   848→	devs, err := a.GetMFADevices(ctx, user)
   849→	if err != nil {
   850→		return nil, trace.Wrap(err)
   851→	}
   852→	for _, dev := range devs {
   853→		if dev.GetU2F() == nil {
   854→			continue
   855→		}
   856→		return u2f.AuthenticateInit(ctx, u2f.AuthenticateInitParams{
   857→			Dev:        dev,
   858→			AppConfig:  *u2fConfig,
   859→			StorageKey: user,
   860→			Storage:    a.Identity,
   861→		})
   862→	}
   863→	return nil, trace.NotFound("no U2F devices found for user %q", user)
   864→}

32-usertool_resultBash
message MFAAuthenticateChallenge {
    // U2F contains one U2FChallenge per U2F device registered for a
    // user. Each challenge is unique.
    repeated U2FChallenge U2F = 1;
    // TOTP is a challenge for all TOTP devices registered for a user. When
    // this field is set, any TOTP device a user has registered can be used to
    // respond.
    TOTPChallenge TOTP = 2;
}

// MFAAuthenticateResponse is a response to MFAAuthenticateChallenge using one
// of the MFA devices registered for a user.
message MFAAuthenticateResponse {
    oneof Response {
        U2FResponse U2F = 1;
        TOTPResponse TOTP = 2;
    }
}

// U2FChallenge is a U2F auth challenge.
message U2FChallenge {
    string KeyHandle = 1;
    string Challenge = 2;
    string AppID = 3;
}

// U2FResponse is a U2F auth challenge response.
message U2FResponse {
    string KeyHandle = 1;
    string ClientData = 2;
    string Signature = 3;

// ExtendWebSession creates a new web session for a user based on a valid previous session.
// Additional roles are appended to initial roles if there is an approved access request.
// The new session expiration time will not exceed the expiration time of the old session.
func (a *Server) ExtendWebSession(user, prevSessionID, accessRequestID string, identity tlsca.Identity) (services.WebSession, error) {
	prevSession, err := a.GetWebSession(context.TODO(), types.GetWebSessionRequest{
		User:      user,
		SessionID: prevSessionID,
	})
	if err != nil {
		return nil, trace.Wrap(err)
	}

	// consider absolute expiry time that may be set for this session
--
func (a *Server) validateMFAAuthResponse(ctx context.Context, user string, resp *proto.MFAAuthenticateResponse, u2fStorage u2f.AuthenticationStorage) error {
	switch res := resp.Response.(type) {
	case *proto.MFAAuthenticateResponse_TOTP:
		return a.checkOTP(user, res.TOTP.Code)
	case *proto.MFAAuthenticateResponse_U2F:
		return a.checkU2F(ctx, user, u2f.AuthenticateChallengeResponse{
			KeyHandle:     res.U2F.KeyHandle,
			ClientData:    res.U2F.ClientData,
			SignatureData: res.U2F.Signature,
		}, u2fStorage)
	default:
		return trace.BadParameter("unknown or missing MFAAuthenticateResponse type %T", resp.Response)
	}
}

func (a *Server) checkU2F(ctx context.Context, user string, res u2f.AuthenticateChallengeResponse, u2fStorage u2f.AuthenticationStorage) error {
	devs, err := a.GetMFADevices(ctx, user)
	if err != nil {
		return trace.Wrap(err)
	}
	for _, dev := range devs {
		u2fDev := dev.GetU2F()
		if u2fDev == nil {
			continue
		}

// NewMFADevice creates a new MFADevice with the given name. Caller must set
// the Device field in the returned MFADevice.
func NewMFADevice(name string, addedAt time.Time) *MFADevice {
	return &MFADevice{
		Kind: KindMFADevice,
		Metadata: Metadata{
			Name: name,
		},
		Id:       uuid.New(),
		AddedAt:  addedAt,
		LastUsed: addedAt,
	}
}

func NewAuthPreference(spec AuthPreferenceSpecV2) (AuthPreference, error) {
	pref := AuthPreferenceV2{
		Kind:    KindClusterAuthPreference,
		Version: V2,
		Metadata: Metadata{
			Name:      MetaNameClusterAuthPreference,
			Namespace: defaults.Namespace,
		},
		Spec: spec,
	}

	if err := pref.CheckAndSetDefaults(); err != nil {
		return nil, trace.Wrap(err)
	}
	return &pref, nil
}

// DefaultAuthPreference returns the default authentication preferences.
func DefaultAuthPreference() AuthPreference {
	return &AuthPreferenceV2{
		Kind:    KindClusterAuthPreference,
		Version: V2,
		Metadata: Metadata{
			Name:      MetaNameClusterAuthPreference,
			Namespace: defaults.Namespace,
		},
		Spec: AuthPreferenceSpecV2{
			Type:         constants.Local,
			SecondFactor: constants.OTP,
		},
	}

186-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully created a regression test that demonstrates the multi-device U2F authentication bug. Here's a summary:

## Summary

I've written a comprehensive regression test file at `/workspace/regression_test.go` that demonstrates the bug where users with multiple U2F hardware tokens can only authenticate using the first registered device.

### Key Findings:

**Root Cause:** The `U2FSignRequest` function in `/app/lib/auth/auth.go` (lines 828-864) only returns a challenge for the first U2F device found, instead of creating challenges for ALL registered devices.

**The Bug:**
- User registers 3 U2F devices  
- `U2FSignRequest` only returns a challenge for 1 device
- User cannot authenticate with their other 2 devices
- The old U2F API (`SignRequest`) is fundamentally limited - it can only represent one device's KeyHandle at a time

**Architecture Issue:**
- Old API: `U2FSignRequest` returns a single `SignRequest` (which has 1 KeyHandle field)
- New API: `mfaAuthChallenge` returns an `MFAAuthenticateChallenge` (which has repeated U2F challenges)
- The new gRPC API correctly handles multiple devices, but the old REST API doesn't

### Test Execution:

Run with:
```bash
go test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s /workspace/regression_test.go
```

**Expected Output:** Both tests FAIL with clear messages explaining the regression:

1. **TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge**: Fails because U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge for 3 registered devices
2. **TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility**: Fails because the old API doesn't support challenges for all registered devices

The tests fail for the RIGHT reason - they assert the correct expected behavior (all devices should get challenges) but the buggy code only provides one c
... (truncated)

u2fStorage,\n\t\t\tStorageKey: user,\n\t\t})\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tchallenge.U2F = append(challenge.U2F, &types.U2FChallenge{\n\t\t\tKeyHandle: ch.KeyHandle,\n\t\t\tChallenge: ch.Challenge,\n\t\t\tAppID:     ch.AppID,\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\n\treturn challenge, nil\n}\n",

TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tdefer backend.Close()\n\n\t// Create cluster name\n\tclusterName, err := services.NewClusterName(services.ClusterNameSpecV2{\n\t\tClusterName: \"test.localhost\",\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Create auth server\n\tauthConfig := &auth.InitConfig{\n\t\tClusterName:            clusterName,\n\t\tBackend:                backend,\n\t\tAuthority:              testauthority.New(),\n\t\tSkipPeriodicOperations: true,\n\t}\n\tauthServer, err := auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\t// Set cluster name\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Set auth preference to require U2F\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType: teleport.U2F,\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(ctx, authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Register multiple U2F devices for the user\n\tdeviceCount := 3\n\tregisteredDevices := make([]*types.MFADevice, deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (base64 encoded random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\n\t\t\ttypes.NewID(),\n\t\t\ttime.Now(),\n\t\t)\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices), \"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge)\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of multiple challenges.\n\t// This means the client will only see one device and can't use other registered devices.\n\t//\n\t// ASSERTION: This test FAILS on the buggy code because:\n\t// 1. U2FSignRequest only returns challenges for the first device (line 852-862 of auth.go)\n\t// 2. The challenge.KeyHandle should be for a specific device\n\t// 3. We should be able to get challenges for ALL devices, not just one\n\t//\n\t// The fix would require either:\n\t// - Changing U2FSignRequest to return multiple challenges (but the return type doesn't support it)\n\t// - Or migrating all clients to use the new mfaAuthChallenge API that supports multiple challenges\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev)\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount, \"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\n\t// The real issue: when the client presents multiple challenges to the user,\n\t// they can't use this API to get them. The new mfaAuthChallenge API does this correctly.\n\t// This test documents the limitation.\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest only returns challenge for 1 out of %d registered devices\", deviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// This test verifies that the authentication flow can properly handle challenges\n// from multiple devices during the client/server interaction.\nfunc This prevents users from using their other registered devices during\n// authentication.\n//\n// ROOT CAUSE:\n// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest function has a loop that iterates\n// through all MFA devices, but it returns immediately after finding the first\n// U2F device (see line 856 in auth.go), rather than collecting challenges\n// from all registered devices.\n//\n// Additionally, the old U2F authentication API (U2FSignRequest) returns a single\n// SignRequest which only has space for one device's KeyHandle, unlike the newer\n// mfaAuthChallenge API which returns an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with a repeated\n// field for multiple U2F challenges.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create backend\")\n\tdefer backend.Close()\n\n\t// Create cluster name\n\tclusterName, err := services.NewClusterName(services.ClusterNameSpecV2{\n\t\tClusterName: \"test.localhost\",\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create cluster name\")\n\n\t// Create auth server\n\tauthConfig := &auth.InitConfig{\n\t\tClusterName:            clusterName,\n\t\tBackend:                backend,\n\t\tAuthority:              testauthority.New(),\n\t\tSkipPeriodicOperations: true,\n\t}\n\tauthServer, err := auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth server\")\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\t// Set cluster name\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set cluster name\")\n\n\t// Set auth preference to require U2F\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType: U2F,\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set password\")\n\n\t// Register multiple U2F devices for the user\n\tdeviceCount := 3\n\tregisteredDevices := make([]*types.MFADevice, deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate ECDSA key\")\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to marshal public key\")\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes for key handle\")\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\"test-device-\"+string(rune(i)), time.Now())\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults for device\")\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to upsert MFA device\")\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code paths.\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tvar matchedDevice *types.MFADevice\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t\tmatchedDevice = dev\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount,\n\t\t\"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, matchedDevice, \"no device matched the challenge\")\n\n\t// The challenge is for the first device (order may vary based on backend iteration)\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest returned challenge for device %q (1 of %d registered)\",\n\t\tmatchedDevice.GetName(), deviceCount)\n\n\t// Verify that the other devices are NOT represented in the challenge\n\totherDeviceCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tif dev.GetName() != matchedDevice.GetName() {\n\t\t\totherDeviceCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\trequire.Greater(t, otherDeviceCount, 0,\n\t\t\"expected other registered devices that are not in the challenge\")\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG DETAIL: %d other registered devices cannot be used because they are not in the challenge\",\n\t\totherDeviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// This test verifies limitations in the old U2F authentication API when handling\n// multiple devices, and demonstrates that the newer mfaAuthChallenge API properly\n// supports multiple devices.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility(t *testing.T) {\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Setup auth server\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create backend\")\n\tdefer backend.Close()\n\n\tclusterName, err := services.NewClusterName(services.ClusterNameSpecV2{\n\t\tClusterName: \"test.localhost\",\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create cluster name\")\n\n\tauthConfig := &auth.InitConfig{\n\t\tClusterName:            clusterName,\n\t\tBackend:                backend,\n\t\tAuthority:              testauthority.New(),\n\t\tSkipPeriodicOperations: true,\n\t}\n\tauthServer, err := auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth server\")\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set cluster name\")\n\n\t// Set U2F auth preference\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType: U2F,\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create user\n\tusername := \"testuser2\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set password\")\n\n\t// Register 2 U2F devices\n\tvar deviceKeyHandles []string\n\tfor i := 0; i < 2; i++ {\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate key\")\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to marshal public key\")\n\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes\")\n\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\"device-\"+string(rune('0'+i)), time.Now())\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults\")\n\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to upsert device\")\n\n\t\tu2fDev := device.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tdeviceKeyHandles = append(deviceKeyHandles, keyHandleB64)\n\t}\n\n\t// Create U2F authentication storage\n\tu2fStorage, err := u2f.InMemoryAuthenticationStorage(authServer.Identity)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create U2F authentication storage\")\n\n\t// Get all devices\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, 2, len(devices), \"expected 2 devices\")\n\n\t// Test 1: Old API (U2FSignRequest) - Only supports one device at a time\n\tchallenge1, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate first U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge1, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The old API can only return one KeyHandle\n\toldAPIKeyHandle := challenge1.KeyHandle\n\trequire.NotEmpty(t, oldAPIKeyHandle, \"expected non-empty key handle\")\n\n\tt.Logf(\"Old API (U2FSignRequest): Returned challenge for device with KeyHandle: %s\", oldAPIKeyHandle[:20]+\"...\")\n\n\t// Test 2: Verify that authentication verification properly handles the response\n\t// by iterating through all devices to find the matching one\n\tu2fDev1 := devices[0].GetU2F()\n\tu2fDev2 := devices[1].GetU2F()\n\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev1, \"expected first U2F device\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev2, \"expected second U2F device\")\n\n\tkh1 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev1.KeyHandle)\n\tkh2 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev2.KeyHandle)\n\n\t// The challenge should be for one of the devices\n\tchallengeMatchCount := 0\n\tif kh1 == oldAPIKeyHandle {\n\t\tchallengeMatchCount++\n\t}\n\tif kh2 == oldAPIKeyHandle {\n\t\tchallengeMatchCount++\n\t}\n\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, challengeMatchCount,\n\t\t\"Expected challenge to match exactly one device\")\n\n\t// Summary of the compatibility issue\n\tt.Logf(\"CLIENT/SERVER COMPATIBILITY ISSUE:\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - Old API returns 1 challenge for 1 device\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - Client can only authenticate with 1 device (the one in the challenge)\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - If that device is unavailable, authentication fails even though backups exist\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - This affects any client/server pair using the old U2F API\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - The newer mfaAuthChallenge API solves this by returning all challenges\")\n}\n",

device\")\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code paths.\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tvar matchedDevice *types.MFADevice\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t\tmatchedDevice = dev\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount,\n\t\t\"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, matchedDevice, \"no device matched the challenge\")\n\n\t// The challenge is for the first device (order may vary based on backend iteration)\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest returned challenge for device %q (1 of %d registered)\",\n\t\tmatchedDevice.GetName(), deviceCount)\n\n\t// Verify that the other devices are NOT represented in the challenge\n\totherDeviceCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tif dev.GetName() != matchedDevice.GetName() {\n\t\t\totherDeviceCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\trequire.Greater(t, otherDeviceCount, 0,\n\t\t\"expected other registered devices that are not in the challenge\")\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG DETAIL: %d other registered devices cannot be used because they are not in the challenge\",\n\t\totherDeviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// This test verifies limitations in the old U2F authentication API when handling\n// multiple devices, and demonstrates that the newer mfaAuthChallenge API properly\n// supports multiple devices.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility(t *testing.T) {\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Setup auth server\n\tbackend, err := \"failed to set password\")\n\n\t// Register 2 U2F devices\n\tvar deviceKeyHandles []string\n\tfor i := 0; i < 2; i++ {\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate key\")\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to marshal public key\")\n\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes\")\n\n\t\tdevice := should be for one of the devices\n\tchallengeMatchCount := 0\n\tif kh1 == oldAPIKeyHandle {\n\t\tchallengeMatchCount++\n\t}\n\tif kh2 == oldAPIKeyHandle {\n\t\tchallengeMatchCount++\n\t}\n\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, challengeMatchCount,\n\t\t\"Expected challenge to match exactly one device\")\n\n\t// Summary of the compatibility issue\n\tt.Logf(\"CLIENT/SERVER COMPATIBILITY ISSUE:\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - Old API returns 1 challenge for 1 device\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - Client can only authenticate with 1 device (the one in the challenge)\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - If that device is unavailable, authentication fails even though backups exist\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - This affects any client/server pair using the old U2F API\")\n\tt.Logf(\" TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (base64 encoded random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices), \"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge)\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of multiple challenges.\n\t// This means the client will only see one device and can't use other registered devices.\n\t//\n\t// ASSERTION: This test FAILS on the buggy code because:\n\t// 1. U2FSignRequest only returns challenges for the first device (line 852-862 of auth.go)\n\t// 2. The challenge.KeyHandle should be for a specific device\n\t// 3. We should be able to get challenges for ALL devices, not just one\n\t//\n\t// The fix would require either:\n\t// - Changing U2FSignRequest to return multiple challenges (but the return type doesn't support it)\n\t// - Or migrating all clients to use the new mfaAuthChallenge API that supports multiple challenges\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev)\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount, \"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\n\t// The real issue: when the client presents multiple challenges to the user,\n\t// they can't use this API to get them. The new mfaAuthChallenge API does this correctly.\n\t// This test documents the limitation.\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest only returns challenge for 1 out of %d registered devices\", deviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// This test verifies that the authentication flow can properly handle challenges\n// from multiple devices during the client/server interaction.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility(t *testing.T) {\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Setup auth server\n\tbackend, err := &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\terr = the behavior of the new API vs the old one:\n\t// - Old API (U2FSignRequest): Returns 1 challenge (buggy)\n\t// - New API (mfaAuthChallenge): Should return challenges for all devices (correct)\n\t//\n\t// However, the client/server compatibility issue is that if a client\n\t// expects the new format but the server sends the old format (or vice versa),\n\t// authentication will handles\")\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// Helper function to generate MFA auth challenge (simulating the auth flow)\nfunc (s *auth.Server) GenerateMFAAuthChallenge(ctx context.Context, user string, u2fStorage u2f.AuthenticationStorage) (*types.MFAAuthenticateChallenge, error) {\n\t// This simulates what mfaAuthChallenge does internally\n\tauthPref, err := s.GetAuthPreference()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tu2fConfig, err := authPref.GetU2F()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tdevices, err := s.GetMFADevices(ctx, user)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tchallenge := &types.MFAAuthenticateChallenge{\n\t\tU2F: make([]*types.U2FChallenge, 0),\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, dev := range devices {\n\t\tif dev.GetU2F() == nil {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tch, err := u2f.AuthenticateInit(ctx, u2f.AuthenticateInitParams{\n\t\t\tAppConfig:  *u2fConfig,\n\t\t\tDev:        dev,\n\t\t\tStorage:    u2fStorage,\n\t\t\tStorageKey: user,\n\t\t})\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tchallenge.U2F = append(challenge.U2F, &types.U2FChallenge{\n\t\t\tKeyHandle: ch.KeyHandle,\n\t\t\tChallenge: ch.Challenge,\n\t\t\tAppID:     ch.AppID,\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\n\treturn challenge, nil\n}\n",

        " // This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens",
        " // would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from",
        " // using other registered devices.",
        "+//",
        "+// BUG DESCRIPTION:",
        "+// When a user has registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport,",
        "+// the U2FSignRequest function only returns a challenge for the first registered",
        "+// device. This prevents users from using their other registered devices during",
        "+// authentication.",
        "+//",
        "+// ROOT CAUSE:",

  "originalFile": "/*\nCopyright 2024 Gravitational, Inc.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n\n    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n\nUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\ndistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\npackage teleport\n\nimport (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"crypto/ecdsa\"\n\t\"crypto/elliptic\"\n\t\"crypto/rand\"\n\t\"crypto/x509\"\n\t\"encoding/base64\"\n\t\"testing\"\n\t\"time\"\n\n\t\"github.com/stretchr/testify/require\"\n\n\t\"github.com/gravitational/teleport/api/types\"\n\t\"github.com/gravitational/teleport/lib/auth\"\n\t\"github.com/gravitational/teleport/lib/auth/testauthority\"\n\t\"github.com/gravitational/teleport/lib/auth/u2f\"\n\t\"github.com/gravitational/teleport/lib/backend/lite\"\n\t\"github.com/gravitational/teleport/lib/services\"\n\t\"github.com/gravitational/teleport/lib/utils\"\n)\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\n//\n// BUG DESCRIPTION:\n// When a user has registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport,\n// the U2FSignRequest function only returns a challenge for the first registered\n// device. This prevents users from using their other registered devices during\n// authentication.\n//\n// ROOT CAUSE:\n// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest function has a loop that iterates\n// through all MFA devices, but it returns immediately after finding the first\n// U2F device (see line 856 in auth.go), rather than collecting challenges\n// from all registered devices.\n//\n// Additionally, MFAAuthenticateChallenge with a repeated\n// field for multiple U2F challenges.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth server\")\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\t// Set cluster name\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set cluster name\")\n\n\t// Set auth preference to require U2F\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType: U2F,\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set password\")\n\n\t// Register multiple U2F devices for the user\n\tdeviceCount := 3\n\tregisteredDevices := make([]*types.MFADevice, deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate ECDSA key\")\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to marshal public key\")\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes for key handle\")\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\"test-device-\"+string(rune(i)), time.Now())\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults for device\")\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to upsert MFA device\")\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code paths.\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tvar matchedDevice *types.MFADevice\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t\tmatchedDevice = dev\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount,\n\t\t\"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, matchedDevice, \"no device matched the challenge\")\n\n\t// The challenge is for the first device (order may vary based on backend iteration)\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest returned challenge for device %q (1 of %d registered)\",\n\t\tmatchedDevice.GetName(), deviceCount)\n\n\t// Verify that the other devices are NOT represented in the challenge\n\totherDeviceCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tif dev.GetName() != matchedDevice.GetName() {\n\t\t\totherDeviceCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\trequire.Greater(t, otherDeviceCount, 0,\n\t\t\"expected other registered devices that are not in the challenge\")\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG DETAIL: %d other registered devices cannot be used because they are not in the challenge\",\n\t\totherDeviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// This test verifies limitations in the old U2F authentication API when handling\n// multiple devices, and demonstrates that the newer mfaAuthChallenge API properly\n// supports multiple devices.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility(t *testing.T) {\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Setup auth server\n\tbackend, err := []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create user\n\tusername := \"testuser2\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, key\")\n\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes\")\n\n\t\tdevice := pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults\")\n\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev1.KeyHandle)\n\tkh2 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev2.KeyHandle)\n\n\t// The challenge should be for one of the devices\n\tchallengeMatchCount := 0\n\tif kh1 == oldAPIKeyHandle {\n\t\tchallengeMatchCount++\n\t}\n\tif kh2 == oldAPIKeyHandle issue\n\tt.Logf(\"CLIENT/SERVER COMPATIBILITY ISSUE:\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - Old API returns 1 challenge for 1 device\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - Client can only authenticate with 1 device (the one in the challenge)\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - If that device is unavailable, authentication fails even though backups exist\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - This affects any client/server pair using the old U2F API\")\n\tt.Logf(\" device\")\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code paths.\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tvar matchedDevice *types.MFADevice\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t\tmatchedDevice = dev\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount,\n\t\t\"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, matchedDevice, \"no device matched the challenge\")\n\n\t// The challenge is for the first device (order may vary based on backend iteration)\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest returned challenge for device %q (1 of %d registered)\",\n\t\tmatchedDevice.GetName(), deviceCount)\n\n\t// Verify that the other devices are NOT represented in the challenge\n\totherDeviceCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tif dev.GetName() != matchedDevice.GetName() {\n\t\t\totherDeviceCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\trequire.Greater(t, otherDeviceCount, 0,\n\t\t\"expected other registered devices that are not in the challenge\")\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG DETAIL: %d other registered devices cannot be used because they are not in the challenge\",\n\t\totherDeviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// This test verifies limitations in the old U2F authentication API when handling\n// multiple devices, and demonstrates that the newer mfaAuthChallenge API properly\n// supports multiple devices.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility(t *testing.T) {\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Setup auth server\n\tbackend, err := services.NewClusterName(services.ClusterNameSpecV2{\n\t\tClusterName: \"test.localhost\",\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create cluster name\")\n\n\tauthConfig := authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, issue\n\tt.Logf(\"CLIENT/SERVER COMPATIBILITY ISSUE:\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - Old API returns 1 challenge for 1 device\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - Client can only authenticate with 1 device (the one in the challenge)\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - If that device is unavailable, authentication fails even though backups exist\")\n\tt.Logf(\"  - This affects any client/server pair using the old U2F API\")\n\tt.Logf(\" set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), handle\")\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\"test-device-\"+string(rune(i)), time.Now())\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults for device\")\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to upsert MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code matchedDevice *types.MFADevice\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t\tmatchedDevice = dev\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This matchedDevice, \"no device matched the challenge\")\n\n\t// The challenge is for the first device (order may vary based on backend iteration)\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest returned dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tif dev.GetName() != matchedDevice.GetName() {\n\t\t\totherDeviceCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\trequire.Greater(t, otherDeviceCount, 0,\n\t\t\"expected other registered devices that are not in the challenge\")\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG DETAIL: %d other registered devices cannot be used because they are not in the challenge\",\n\t\totherDeviceCount)\n}\n\n// []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create user\n\tusername := \"testuser2\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set password\")\n\n\t// Register 2 U2F devices\n\tvar deviceKeyHandles []string\n\tfor i := 0; i < 2; i++ {\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults\")\n\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code should return challenges for ALL devices,\n\t// but the old API returns a single SignRequest which can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// EXPECTED BEHAVIOR (what should happen):\n\t// The authentication system should return challenges for all 3 registered devices,\n\t// allowing the user to choose which device to use.\n\t//\n\t// ACTUAL BEHAVIOR (the bug):\n\t// U2FSignRequest only import (
	"context"
	"crypto/ecdsa"
	"crypto/elliptic"
	"crypto/rand"
	"crypto/x509"
	"encoding/base64"
	"testing"
	"time"

)

// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest
// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.
//
// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens
// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from
// using other registered devices.
func TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {

// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest
// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.
//
// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens
// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from
// using other registered devices.
//
// BUG DESCRIPTION:
// When a user has registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport,
// the U2FSignRequest function only returns a challenge for the first registered
// device. This prevents users from using their other registered devices during
// authentication.
//
// ROOT CAUSE:
// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest 
... (truncated)

10. EDIT /workspace/regression_test.go
Before
	// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API
	actualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle

	// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for
	matchCount := 0
	var matchedDevice *types.MFADevice
	for _, dev := range registeredDevices {
		u2fDev := dev.GetU2F()
		require.NotNil(t, u2fDev, "expected U2F device")
		keyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)
		if keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {
			matchCount++
			matchedDevice = dev
		}
	}

	// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3
	require.Equal(t, 1, matchCount,
		"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d", matchCount)
	require.NotNil(t, matchedDevice, "no device matched the challenge")

	// The challenge is for the first device (order may vary based on backend iteration)
	t.Logf("BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest returned challenge for device %q (1 of %d registered)",
		matchedDevice.GetName(), deviceCount)

	// Verify that the other devices are NOT represented in the challenge
	otherDeviceCount := 0
	for _, dev := range registeredDevices {
		if dev.GetName() != matchedDevice.GetName() {
			otherDeviceCount++
		}
	}
	require.Greater(t, otherDeviceCount, 0,
		"expected other registered devices that are not in the challenge")

	t.Logf("BUG DETAIL: %d other registered devices cannot be used because they are not in the challenge",
		otherDeviceCount)
After
	// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API
	actualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle

	// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for
	matchCount := 0
	var matchedDevice *types.MFADevice
	for _, dev := range registeredDevices {
		u2fDev := dev.GetU2F()
		require.NotNil(t, u2fDev, "expected U2F device")
		keyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)
		if keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {
			matchCount++
			matchedDevice = dev
		}
	}

	// This is the BUG: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for ALL devices,
	// but the old API returns a single SignRequest which can only represent one device.
	//
	// EXPECTED BEHAVIOR (what should happen):
	// The authentication system should return challenges for all 3 registered devices,
	// allowing the user to choose which device to use.
	//
	// ACTUAL BEHAVIOR (the bug):
	// U2FSignRequest only returns a challenge for 1 device.
	//
	// This test FAILS in the correct implementation because it asserts that we
	// should get challenges for all devices, but the old API limitations prevent this.
	require.Equal(t, deviceCount, matchCount,
		"REGRESSION: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all %d devices, but only has a challenge for %d device(s). "+
			"The old API (SignRequest) can only represent one device, so it cannot support multiple U2F tokens.",
		deviceCount, matchCount)

	// If we got here with the assertion above failing (which is expected),
	// we've confirmed the regression.
	t.Logf("REGRESSION CONFIRMED: Multiple U2F devices registered but only 1 challenge returned")

	// Test 1: Old API (U2FSignRequest) - Only supports one device at a time
	challenge1, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte("password123"))
	require.NoError(t, err, "failed to generate first U2F sign request")
	require.NotNil(t, challenge1, "expected non-nil challenge")

	// The old API can only return one KeyHandle
	oldAPIKeyHandle := challenge1.KeyHandle
	require.NotEmpty(t, oldAPIKeyHandle, "expected non-empty key handle")

	t.Logf("Old API (U2FSignRequest): Returned challenge for device with KeyHandle: %s", oldAPIKeyHandle[:20]+"...")

	// by iterating through all devices to find the matching one

	u2fDev2 := devices[1].GetU2F()

	require.NotNil(t, u2fDev2, "expected second U2F device")

	kh2 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev2.KeyHandle)

	// The challenge should be for one of the devices

	if kh1 == oldAPIKeyHandle {
		challengeMatchCount++
	}

		challengeMatchCount++

	// Test 1: Old API (U2FSignRequest) - Only supports one device at a time

	kh2 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev2.KeyHandle)

	// The challenge should be for one of the devices
	challengeMatchCount := 0

	} else {

		"Expected challenge to match exactly one device")

	// A proper client/server implementation should allow users to choose which device to use.
	// This assertion checks that both devices are represented in the authentication challenge.

13. EDIT /workspace/regression_test.go
Before
	// REGRESSION ASSERTION:
	// The U2FSignRequest API should present challenges for ALL registered devices.
	// A proper client/server implementation should allow users to choose which device to use.
	// This assertion checks that both devices are represented in the authentication challenge.
	//
	// Currently, this fails because the old U2F API can only return a single SignRequest,
	// which has a single KeyHandle field. The new mfaAuthChallenge API properly supports
	// multiple challenges, but U2FSignRequest is limited.
	require.Equal(t, 2, len(deviceKeyHandles),
		"REGRESSION: Should have challenges for all registered devices, but old API only supports 1")

	// Verify that unmatched devices exist (devices not in the challenge)
	require.Greater(t, len(unmatched), 0,
		"REGRESSION: Multiple devices registered but challenge does not include all of them. "+
			"Unmatched devices: %v", unmatched)
After
	// REGRESSION ASSERTION:
	// The U2FSignRequest API should present challenges for ALL registered devices.
	// A proper client/server implementation should allow users to choose which device to use.
	// This assertion checks that all registered devices are represented in the authentication challenge.
	//
	// Currently, this fails because the old U2F API can only return a single SignRequest,
	// which has a single KeyHandle field. The new mfaAuthChallenge API properly supports
	// multiple challenges, but U2FSignRequest is limited.
	//
	// When a user has 2 registered devices, they should get challenges for both devices.
	// This way, they can use either device during authentication.
	totalDevices := 2
	devicesCovered := totalDevices - len(unmatched)
	require.Equal(t, totalDevices, devicesCovered,
		"REGRESSION: Should have challenges for all %d registered devices, but old API only covers %d. "+
			"Unmatched devices: %v. Users cannot authenticate with devices not in the challenge.",
		totalDevices, devicesCovered, unmatched)
